a{background:url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg")right 0.1em center/12px no-repeat}body:not(.skin-timeless):not(.skin-minerva) .mw-parser-output .id-lock-free a,body:not(.skin-timeless):not(.skin-minerva) .mw-parser-output .id-lock-limited a,body:not(.skin-timeless):not(.skin-minerva) .mw-parser-output .id-lock-registration a,body:not(.skin-timeless):not(.skin-minerva) .mw-parser-output .id-lock-subscription a,body:not(.skin-timeless):not(.skin-minerva) .mw-parser-output .cs1-ws-icon a{background-size:contain;padding:0 1em 0 0}.mw-parser-output .cs1-code{color:inherit;background:inherit;border:none;padding:inherit}.mw-parser-output .cs1-hidden-error{display:none;color:var(--color-error,#d33)}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-right{padding-right:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .citation .mw-selflink{font-weight:inherit}@media screen{.mw-parser-output .cs1-format{font-size:95%}html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .cs1-maint{color:#18911f}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .cs1-maint{color:#18911f}}</style><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc8259">8259</a>), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ecma-international.org/publications-and-standards/standards/ecma-404/">ECMA-404</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.iso.org/standard/71616.html">ISO/IEC 21778:2017</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="line-height: 1.2; padding-right: 0.65em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Open_file_format" title="Open file format">Open format</a>?</span></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height: 1.35;">Yes</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="line-height: 1.2; padding-right: 0.65em;">Website</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height: 1.35;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://json.org/">json<wbr />.org</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>JSON</b> (<b>JavaScript Object Notation</b>, pronounced <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/dʒ/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">dʒ</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ən/: &#39;on&#39; in &#39;button&#39;">ən</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/dʒ/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">dʒ</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ɒ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">ɒ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is an <a href="/wiki/Open_standard" title="Open standard">open standard</a> file format and <a href="/wiki/Electronic_data_interchange" title="Electronic data interchange">data interchange</a> format that uses <a href="/wiki/Human-readable" class="mw-redirect" title="Human-readable">human-readable</a> text to store and transmit data objects consisting of <a href="/wiki/Name%E2%80%93value_pair" title="Name–value pair">name–value pairs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Array_data_type" class="mw-redirect" title="Array data type">arrays</a> (or other <a href="/wiki/Serialization" title="Serialization">serializable</a> values). It is a commonly used data format with diverse  uses in <a href="/wiki/Electronic_data_interchange" title="Electronic data interchange">electronic data interchange</a>, including that of <a href="/wiki/Web_application" title="Web application">web applications</a> with <a href="/wiki/Server_(computing)" title="Server (computing)">servers</a>.
</p><p>JSON is a <a href="/wiki/Language-independent_specification" title="Language-independent specification">language-independent</a> data format. It was derived from <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>, but many modern <a href="/wiki/Programming_language" title="Programming language">programming languages</a> include code to generate and <a href="/wiki/Parse" class="mw-redirect" title="Parse">parse</a> JSON-format data. JSON filenames use the extension <code>.json</code>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Douglas_Crockford" title="Douglas Crockford">Douglas Crockford</a> originally specified the JSON format in the early 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-saga_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saga-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He and <a href="/wiki/Chip_Morningstar" title="Chip Morningstar">Chip Morningstar</a> sent the first JSON message in April 2001.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Naming_and_pronunciation">Naming and pronunciation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Naming and pronunciation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The 2017 <a href="/wiki/International_standard" title="International standard">international standard</a> (ECMA-404 and ISO/IEC 21778:2017) specifies that "JSON" is "pronounced <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/dʒ/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">dʒ</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="/./: syllable break">.</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>, as in '<a href="/wiki/Jason" title="Jason">Jason</a> and The <a href="/wiki/Argonauts" title="Argonauts">Argonauts</a><span style="padding-right:.15em;">'</span>".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ecma2017_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecma2017-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The first (2013) edition of ECMA-404 did not address the pronunciation.<sup id="cite_ref-ecma2013_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecma2013-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <i>UNIX and Linux System Administration Handbook</i> states, "<a href="/wiki/Douglas_Crockford" title="Douglas Crockford">Douglas Crockford</a>, who named and promoted the JSON format, says it's pronounced like the name Jason. But somehow, 'JAY-sawn'<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> seems to have become more common in the technical community."<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Crockford said in 2011, "There's a lot of argument about how you pronounce that, but I strictly don't care."<sup id="cite_ref-saga_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saga-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Standards">Standards</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Standards"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>After RFC 4627 had been available as its "informational" specification since 2006, JSON was first standardized in 2013, as <a href="/wiki/Ecma_International" title="Ecma International">ECMA</a>-404.<sup id="cite_ref-ecma2013_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecma2013-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> RFC 8259, published in 2017, is the current version of the <a href="/wiki/Internet_Standard" title="Internet Standard">Internet Standard</a> STD 90, and it remains consistent with ECMA-404.<sup id="cite_ref-rfc8259_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc8259-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> That same year, JSON was also standardized as <a href="/wiki/ISO/IEC" class="mw-redirect" title="ISO/IEC">ISO/IEC</a> 21778:2017.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ecma_International" title="Ecma International">ECMA</a> and <a href="/wiki/ISO/IEC" class="mw-redirect" title="ISO/IEC">ISO/IEC</a> standards describe only the allowed syntax, whereas the RFC covers some security and interoperability considerations.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_Crockford.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Douglas_Crockford.jpg/220px-Douglas_Crockford.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Douglas_Crockford.jpg/330px-Douglas_Crockford.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Douglas_Crockford.jpg/440px-Douglas_Crockford.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2560" /></a><figcaption>Douglas Crockford at the Yahoo Building (2007)</figcaption></figure>
<p>JSON grew out of a need for a real-time server-to-browser session communication protocol without using browser plugins such as <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash" title="Adobe Flash">Flash</a> or <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a> applets, the dominant methods used in the early 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-Edu4java,_2014_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edu4java,_2014-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Crockford first specified and popularized the JSON format.<sup id="cite_ref-saga_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saga-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The acronym originated at State Software, a company cofounded by Crockford and others in March 2001. The cofounders agreed to build a system that used standard browser capabilities and provided an <a href="/wiki/Abstraction_layer" title="Abstraction layer">abstraction layer</a> for Web developers to create stateful Web applications that had a persistent duplex connection to a Web server by holding two <a href="/wiki/Hypertext_Transfer_Protocol" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypertext Transfer Protocol">Hypertext Transfer Protocol</a> (HTTP) connections open and recycling them before standard browser time-outs if no further data were exchanged. The cofounders had a round-table discussion and voted on whether to call the data format JSML (JavaScript Markup Language) or JSON (JavaScript Object Notation), as well as under what <a href="/wiki/Software_license" title="Software license">license</a> type to make it available. The JSON.org<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> website was launched in 2001. In December 2005, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a> began offering some of its <a href="/wiki/Web_service" title="Web service">Web services</a> in JSON.<sup id="cite_ref-yahoo_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A precursor to the JSON libraries was used in a children's digital asset trading game project named <a href="/wiki/Cartoon_Orbit" title="Cartoon Orbit">Cartoon Orbit</a> at Communities.com <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  which used a browser side plug-in with a proprietary messaging format to manipulate <a href="/wiki/DHTML" class="mw-redirect" title="DHTML">DHTML</a> elements. Upon discovery of early <a href="/wiki/Ajax_(programming)" title="Ajax (programming)">Ajax</a> capabilities, digiGroups, Noosh, and others used frames to pass information into the user browsers' visual field without refreshing a Web application's visual context, realizing real-time rich Web applications using only the standard HTTP, HTML, and JavaScript capabilities of Netscape 4.0.5+ and Internet Explorer 5+. Crockford then found that JavaScript could be used as an object-based messaging format for such a system. The system was sold to <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Data_Systems" title="Electronic Data Systems">EDS</a>.
</p><p>JSON was based on a <a href="/wiki/Subset" title="Subset">subset</a> of the <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a> scripting language (specifically, Standard <a href="/wiki/Ecma_International" title="Ecma International">ECMA</a>-262 3rd Edition—December 1999<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>) and is commonly used with JavaScript, but it is a <a href="/wiki/Language-independent_specification" title="Language-independent specification">language-independent</a> data format. Code for <a href="/wiki/Parsing" title="Parsing">parsing</a> and generating JSON data is readily available in many <a href="/wiki/Programming_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Programming languages">programming languages</a>. JSON's website lists JSON <a href="/wiki/Language_binding" title="Language binding">libraries</a> by language.
</p><p>In October 2013, <a href="/wiki/Ecma_International" title="Ecma International">Ecma International</a> published the first edition of its JSON standard ECMA-404.<sup id="cite_ref-ecma2013_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecma2013-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> That same year, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc7158">7158</a> used ECMA-404 as a reference. In 2014, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc7159">7159</a> became the main reference for JSON's Internet uses, superseding <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc4627">4627</a> and <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc7158">7158</a> (but preserving ECMA-262 and ECMA-404 as main references). In November 2017, <a href="/wiki/ISO/IEC_JTC_1/SC_22" title="ISO/IEC JTC 1/SC 22">ISO/IEC JTC 1/SC 22</a> published ISO/IEC 21778:2017<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> as an international standard. On December 13, 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Internet_Engineering_Task_Force" title="Internet Engineering Task Force">Internet Engineering Task Force</a> obsoleted <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc7159">7159</a> when it published <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc8259">8259</a>, which is the current version of the <a href="/wiki/Internet_Standard" title="Internet Standard">Internet Standard</a> STD 90.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Crockford added a clause to the JSON license stating, "The Software shall be used for Good, not Evil", in order to <a href="/wiki/Open-source" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source">open-source</a> the JSON libraries while mocking corporate lawyers and those who are overly pedantic. On the other hand, this clause led to <a href="/wiki/License_compatibility" title="License compatibility">license compatibility</a> problems of the JSON license with other <a href="/wiki/Open-source_license" title="Open-source license">open-source licenses</a> since <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source software</a> and <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">free software</a> usually imply no restrictions on the purpose of use.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Syntax">Syntax</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Syntax"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The following example shows a possible JSON representation describing a person.
</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-json mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="nt">&quot;first_name&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;John&quot;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="nt">&quot;last_name&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;Smith&quot;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="nt">&quot;is_alive&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">true</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="nt">&quot;age&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">27</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="nt">&quot;address&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="nt">&quot;street_address&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;21 2nd Street&quot;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="nt">&quot;city&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;New York&quot;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="nt">&quot;state&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;NY&quot;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="nt">&quot;postal_code&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;10021-3100&quot;</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="p">},</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="nt">&quot;phone_numbers&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">      </span><span class="nt">&quot;type&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;home&quot;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">      </span><span class="nt">&quot;number&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;212 555-1234&quot;</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="p">},</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">      </span><span class="nt">&quot;type&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;office&quot;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">      </span><span class="nt">&quot;number&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;646 555-4567&quot;</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="p">}</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="p">],</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="nt">&quot;children&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="s2">&quot;Catherine&quot;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="s2">&quot;Thomas&quot;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="s2">&quot;Trevor&quot;</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="p">],</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="nt">&quot;spouse&quot;</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">null</span>
<span class="p">}</span>
</pre></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Character_encoding">Character encoding</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Character encoding"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Although Crockford originally asserted that JSON is a strict subset of <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a> and <a href="/wiki/ECMAScript" title="ECMAScript">ECMAScript</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> his specification actually allows valid JSON documents that are not valid JavaScript; JSON allows the <a href="/wiki/Unicode#Newlines" title="Unicode">Unicode line terminators</a> <span class="nowrap"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">U+2028</span>&#x20;</span> <span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase; font-feature-settings: &#39;onum&#39;">LINE SEPARATOR</span> and <span class="nowrap"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">U+2029</span>&#x20;</span> <span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase; font-feature-settings: &#39;onum&#39;">PARAGRAPH SEPARATOR</span> to appear unescaped in quoted strings, while ECMAScript 2018 and older do not.<sup id="cite_ref-json-2028_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-json-2028-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ECMATC39_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECMATC39-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This is a consequence of JSON disallowing only "control characters". For maximum portability, these characters are backslash-escaped.
</p><p>JSON exchange in an open ecosystem must be encoded in <a href="/wiki/UTF-8" title="UTF-8">UTF-8</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rfc8259_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc8259-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The encoding supports the full Unicode character set, including those characters outside the <a href="/wiki/Basic_Multilingual_Plane" class="mw-redirect" title="Basic Multilingual Plane">Basic Multilingual Plane</a> (U+0000 to U+FFFF). However, if escaped, those characters must be written using <a href="/wiki/UTF-16#Code_points_from_U+010000_to_U+10FFFF" title="UTF-16">UTF-16 surrogate pairs</a>. For example, to include the <a href="/wiki/Emoji" title="Emoji">Emoji</a> character <span class="nowrap"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">U+1F610</span>&#x20;</span><span style="font-size:125%;line-height:1em">&#x1f610;</span> <span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase; font-feature-settings: &#39;onum&#39;">NEUTRAL FACE</span> in JSON:
</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-javascript mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;face&quot;</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;😐&quot;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span>
<span class="c1">// or</span>
<span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;face&quot;</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">&quot;\uD83D\uDE10&quot;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span>
</pre></div>
<p>JSON became a strict subset of ECMAScript as of the language's 2019 revision.<sup id="cite_ref-ECMATC39_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECMATC39-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ECMATC39Stage4_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECMATC39Stage4-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Data_types">Data types</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Data types"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>JSON's basic data types are:
</p>
<ul><li>Number: a signed decimal number that may contain a fractional part and may use exponential <a href="/wiki/E_notation" class="mw-redirect" title="E notation">E notation</a> but cannot include non-numbers such as <a href="/wiki/NaN" title="NaN">NaN</a>. The format makes no distinction between integer and floating-point. JavaScript uses <a href="/wiki/IEEE-754" class="mw-redirect" title="IEEE-754">IEEE-754</a> <a href="/wiki/Double-precision_floating-point_format" title="Double-precision floating-point format">double-precision floating-point format</a> for all its numeric values (later also supporting <a href="/wiki/Arbitrary-precision_arithmetic" title="Arbitrary-precision arithmetic">BigInt</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>), but other languages implementing JSON may encode numbers differently.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/String_(computer_science)" title="String (computer science)">String</a>: a sequence of <a href="/wiki/Empty_string" title="Empty string">zero</a> or more <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> characters. Strings are delimited with double quotation marks and support a backslash <a href="/wiki/Escape_character" title="Escape character">escaping</a> syntax.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Boolean_data_type" title="Boolean data type">Boolean</a>: either of the values <code>true</code> or <code>false</code></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Array_data_structure" class="mw-redirect" title="Array data structure">Array</a>: an <a href="/wiki/List_(abstract_data_type)" title="List (abstract data type)">ordered list</a> of zero or more elements, each of which may be of any type. Arrays use <a href="/wiki/Square_bracket" class="mw-redirect" title="Square bracket">square bracket</a> notation with comma-separated elements.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Object_(computer_science)" title="Object (computer science)">Object</a>: a collection of <a href="/wiki/Name%E2%80%93value_pair" title="Name–value pair">name–value pairs</a> where the names (also called keys) are strings. The current ECMA standard states, "The JSON syntax does not impose any restrictions on the strings used as names, does not require that name strings be unique, and does not assign any significance to the ordering of name/value pairs."<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Objects are delimited with <a href="/wiki/Braces_(punctuation)#Braces" class="mw-redirect" title="Braces (punctuation)">curly brackets</a> and use commas to separate each pair, while within each pair, the colon ':' character separates the key or name from its value.</li>
<li><code><a href="/wiki/Nullable_type" title="Nullable type">null</a></code>: an empty value, using the word <code>null</code></li></ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Whitespace_character" title="Whitespace character">Whitespace</a> is allowed and ignored around or between syntactic elements (values and punctuation, but not within a string value). Four specific characters are considered whitespace for this purpose: <a href="/wiki/Space_(punctuation)" title="Space (punctuation)">space</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horizontal_tab" class="mw-redirect" title="Horizontal tab">horizontal tab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Line_feed" class="mw-redirect" title="Line feed">line feed</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carriage_return" title="Carriage return">carriage return</a>. In particular, the <a href="/wiki/Byte_order_mark" title="Byte order mark">byte order mark</a> must not be generated by a conforming implementation (though it may be accepted when parsing JSON). JSON does not provide syntax for <a href="/wiki/Comment_(computer_programming)" title="Comment (computer programming)">comments</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DouglasCrockfordComments_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DouglasCrockfordComments-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Early versions of JSON (such as specified by <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc4627">4627</a>) required that a valid JSON text must consist of only an object or an array type, which could contain other types within them. This restriction was dropped in <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><a href="/wiki/RFC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="RFC (identifier)">RFC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc7158">7158</a>, where a JSON text was redefined as any serialized value.
</p><p>Numbers in JSON are agnostic with regard to their representation within programming languages. While this allows for numbers of <a href="/wiki/Arbitrary_precision" class="mw-redirect" title="Arbitrary precision">arbitrary precision</a> to be serialized, it may lead to portability issues. For example, since no differentiation is made between integer and floating-point values, some implementations may treat <code>42</code>, <code>42.0</code>, and <code>4.2E+1</code> as the same number, while others may not. The JSON standard makes no requirements regarding implementation details such as <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic_overflow" class="mw-redirect" title="Arithmetic overflow">overflow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Underflow" class="mw-redirect" title="Underflow">underflow</a>, loss of precision, rounding, or <a href="/wiki/Signed_zeros" class="mw-redirect" title="Signed zeros">signed zeros</a>, but it does recommend expecting no more than <a href="/wiki/IEEE_754" title="IEEE 754">IEEE 754</a> <a href="/wiki/Binary64" class="mw-redirect" title="Binary64">binary64</a> precision for "good interoperability". There is no inherent precision loss in serializing a machine-level binary representation of a floating-point number (like binary64) into a human-readable decimal representation (like numbers in JSON) and back since there exist published algorithms to do this exactly and optimally.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Comments were intentionally excluded from JSON. In 2012, Douglas Crockford described his design decision thus: "I removed comments from JSON because I saw people were using them to hold parsing directives, a practice which would have destroyed interoperability."<sup id="cite_ref-DouglasCrockfordComments_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DouglasCrockfordComments-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>JSON disallows "trailing commas", a <a href="/wiki/Comma#Computing" title="Comma">comma</a> after the last value inside a data structure.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Trailing commas are a common feature of <a href="#Derivatives">JSON derivatives</a> to improve ease of use.<sup id="cite_ref-json5_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-json5-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Interoperability">Interoperability</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Interoperability"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>RFC 8259 describes certain aspects of JSON syntax that, while legal per the specifications, can cause interoperability problems.
</p>
<ul><li>Certain JSON implementations only accept JSON texts representing an object or an array. For interoperability, applications interchanging JSON should transmit messages that are objects or arrays.</li>
<li>The specifications allow JSON objects that contain multiple members with the same name. The behavior of implementations processing objects with duplicate names is unpredictable. For interoperability, applications should avoid duplicate names when transmitting JSON objects.</li>
<li>The specifications specifically say that the order of members in JSON objects is not significant. For interoperability, applications should avoid assigning meaning to member ordering even if the parsing software makes that ordering visible.</li>
<li>While the specifications place no limits on the magnitude or precisions of JSON number literals, the widely used JavaScript implementation stores them as IEEE754 "binary64" quantities. For interoperability, applications should avoid transmitting numbers that cannot be represented in this way, for example, 1E400 or 3.141592653589793238462643383279.</li>
<li>While the specifications do not constrain the character encoding of the Unicode characters in a JSON text, the vast majority of implementations assume <a href="/wiki/UTF-8" title="UTF-8">UTF-8</a> encoding; for interoperability, applications should always and only encode JSON messages in UTF-8.</li>
<li>The specifications do not forbid transmitting byte sequences that incorrectly represent Unicode characters. For interoperability, applications should transmit messages containing no such byte sequences.</li>
<li>The specification does not constrain how applications go about comparing Unicode strings. For interoperability, applications should always perform such comparisons code unit by code unit.</li></ul>
<p>In 2015, the IETF published RFC 7493, describing the "I-JSON Message Format", a restricted profile of JSON that constrains the syntax and processing of JSON to avoid, as much as possible, these interoperability issues.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Semantics">Semantics</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Semantics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>While JSON provides a syntactic framework for data interchange, unambiguous data interchange also requires agreement between producer and consumer on the semantics of specific use of the JSON syntax.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One example of where such an agreement is necessary is the serialization of data types that are not part of the JSON standard, for example, dates and <a href="/wiki/Regular_expression" title="Regular expression">regular expressions</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Metadata_and_schema">Metadata and schema</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Metadata and schema"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The official <a href="/wiki/MIME_type" class="mw-redirect" title="MIME type">MIME type</a> for JSON text is <code>application/json</code>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and most modern implementations have adopted this. Legacy MIME types include <code>text/json</code>, <code>text/x-json</code>, and <code>text/javascript</code>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  The standard filename extension is .json.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><i>JSON Schema</i> specifies a JSON-based format to define the structure of JSON data for validation, documentation, and interaction control. It provides a contract for the JSON data required by a given application and how that data can be modified.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> JSON Schema is based on the concepts from <a href="/wiki/XML_Schema_(W3C)" title="XML Schema (W3C)">XML Schema</a> (XSD) but is JSON-based. As in XSD, the same serialization/deserialization tools can be used both for the schema and data, and it is self-describing. It is specified in an <a href="/wiki/Internet_Draft" title="Internet Draft">Internet Draft</a> at the IETF, with the latest version as of 2024 being "Draft 2020-12".<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are several validators available for different programming languages,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> each with varying levels of conformance.
</p><p>The JSON standard does not support object <a href="/wiki/Reference_(computer_science)" title="Reference (computer science)">references</a>, but an <a href="/wiki/IETF" class="mw-redirect" title="IETF">IETF</a> draft standard for JSON-based object references exists.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Uses">Uses</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Uses"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/JSON-RPC" title="JSON-RPC">JSON-RPC</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Remote_procedure_call" title="Remote procedure call">remote procedure call</a> (RPC) protocol built on JSON, as a replacement for <a href="/wiki/XML-RPC" title="XML-RPC">XML-RPC</a> or <a href="/wiki/SOAP" title="SOAP">SOAP</a>. It is a simple protocol that defines only a handful of data types and commands. JSON-RPC lets a system send notifications (information to the server that does not require a response) and multiple calls to the server that can be answered out of order.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Asynchronous_JavaScript_and_JSON" class="mw-redirect" title="Asynchronous JavaScript and JSON">Asynchronous JavaScript and JSON</a> (or AJAJ) refers to the same <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_web_page" title="Dynamic web page">dynamic web page</a> methodology as <a href="/wiki/Ajax_(programming)" title="Ajax (programming)">Ajax</a>, but instead of <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a>, JSON is the data format. AJAJ is a web development technique that provides for the ability of a <a href="/wiki/Web_page" title="Web page">web page</a> to request new data after it has loaded into the <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browser</a>. Typically, it renders new data from the server in response to user actions on that web page. For example, what the user types into a <a href="/wiki/Text_box" title="Text box">search box</a>, <a href="/wiki/Client-side_scripting" class="mw-redirect" title="Client-side scripting">client-side code</a> then sends to the server, which immediately responds with a <a href="/wiki/Drop-down_list" title="Drop-down list">drop-down list</a> of matching <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">database</a> items.
</p><p>JSON has seen <a href="/wiki/Ad_hoc" title="Ad hoc">ad hoc</a> usage as a <a href="/wiki/Configuration_file" title="Configuration file">configuration language</a>. However, it does not support <a href="/wiki/Comment_(computer_programming)" title="Comment (computer programming)">comments</a>.
In 2012, Douglas Crockford, JSON creator, had this to say about comments in JSON when used as a configuration language: "I know that the lack of comments makes some people sad, but it shouldn't. Suppose you are using JSON to keep configuration files, which you would like to annotate. Go ahead and insert all the comments you like. Then pipe it through JSMin<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> before handing it to your JSON parser."<sup id="cite_ref-DouglasCrockfordComments_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DouglasCrockfordComments-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/MongoDB" title="MongoDB">MongoDB</a> uses JSON-like data for its <a href="/wiki/Document-oriented_database" title="Document-oriented database">document-oriented database</a>.
</p><p>Some relational databases, such as PostgreSQL and MySQL, have added support for native JSON data types. This allows developers to store JSON data directly in a relational database without having to convert it to another data format.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Safety">Safety</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Safety"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>JSON being a subset of JavaScript can lead to the misconception that it is safe to pass JSON texts to the JavaScript <code><a href="/wiki/Eval" title="Eval">eval</a>()</code> function. This is not safe, due to certain valid JSON texts, specifically those containing <span class="nowrap"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">U+2028</span>&#x20;</span> <span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase; font-feature-settings: &#39;onum&#39;">LINE SEPARATOR</span> or <span class="nowrap"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886049734" /><span class="monospaced">U+2029</span>&#x20;</span> <span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase; font-feature-settings: &#39;onum&#39;">PARAGRAPH SEPARATOR</span>, not being valid JavaScript code until JavaScript specifications were updated in 2019, and so older engines may not support it.<sup id="cite_ref-Magnus_Holm_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Magnus_Holm-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> To avoid the many pitfalls caused by executing arbitrary code from the Internet, a new function, <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-javascript mw-content-ltr" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="nb">JSON</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nx">parse</span><span class="p">()</span></code>, was first added to the fifth edition of ECMAScript,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which as of 2017 is supported by all major browsers. For non-supported browsers, an API-compatible JavaScript library is provided by <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Crockford" title="Douglas Crockford">Douglas Crockford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In addition, the TC39 proposal "Subsume JSON" made <a href="/wiki/ECMAScript" title="ECMAScript">ECMAScript</a> a strict JSON superset as of the language's 2019 revision.<sup id="cite_ref-ECMATC39_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECMATC39-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ECMATC39Stage4_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECMATC39Stage4-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Various JSON parser implementations have suffered from <a href="/wiki/Denial-of-service_attack" title="Denial-of-service attack">denial-of-service attack</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mass_assignment_vulnerability" title="Mass assignment vulnerability">mass assignment vulnerability</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Alternatives">Alternatives</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Alternatives"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_data-serialization_formats" title="Comparison of data-serialization formats">Comparison of data-serialization formats</a></div>
<p>JSON is promoted as a low-overhead alternative to XML as both of these formats have widespread support for creation, reading, and decoding in the real-world situations where they are commonly used.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Apart from XML, examples could include <a href="/wiki/Comma-separated_values" title="Comma-separated values">CSV</a> and <a href="#Supersets">supersets</a> of JSON. <a href="/wiki/Google_Protocol_Buffers" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Protocol Buffers">Google Protocol Buffers</a> can fill this role, although it is not a data interchange language. <a href="/wiki/CBOR" title="CBOR">CBOR</a> has a superset of the JSON data types, but it is not text-based. <a href="/wiki/Ion_(serialization_format)" title="Ion (serialization format)"> Ion</a> is also a superset of JSON, with a wider range of primary types, annotations, comments, and allowing trailing commas.<sup id="cite_ref-ion_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ion-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="XML">XML</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: XML"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> has been used to describe structured data and to serialize objects. Various XML-based protocols exist to represent the same kind of data structures as JSON for the same kind of data interchange purposes. Data can be encoded in XML in several ways. The most expansive form using tag pairs results in a much larger (in character count) representation than JSON, but if data is stored in attributes and 'short tag' form where the closing tag is replaced with <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" style="" dir="ltr">/&gt;</code>, the representation is often about the same size as JSON or just a little larger. However, an XML attribute can only have a single value and each attribute can appear at most once on each element.
</p><p>XML separates "data" from "metadata" (via the use of elements and attributes), while JSON does not have such a concept.
</p><p>Another key difference is the addressing of values. JSON has objects with a simple "key" to "value" mapping, whereas in XML addressing happens on "nodes", which all receive a unique ID via the XML processor. Additionally, the XML standard defines a common attribute <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" style="" dir="ltr">xml:id</code>, that can be used by the user, to set an ID explicitly.
</p><p>XML tag names cannot contain any of the characters <code>!"#$%&amp;'()*+,/;&lt;=&gt;?@[\]^`{|}~</code>, nor a space character, and cannot begin with <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" style="" dir="ltr">-</code>, <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" style="" dir="ltr">.</code>, or a numeric digit, whereas JSON keys can (even if quotation mark and backslash must be escaped).<sup id="cite_ref-XML_1.1_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XML_1.1-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>XML values are strings of <i>characters</i>, with no built-in <a href="/wiki/Type_safety" title="Type safety">type safety</a>. XML has the concept of <a href="/wiki/XML_schema" title="XML schema">schema</a>, that permits strong typing, user-defined types, predefined tags, and formal structure, allowing for formal validation of an XML stream. JSON has several types built-in and has a similar schema concept in <a href="#Metadata_and_schema">JSON Schema</a>.
</p><p>XML supports comments, while JSON does not.<sup id="cite_ref-Saternos45_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saternos45-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DouglasCrockfordComments_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DouglasCrockfordComments-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Supersets">Supersets</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Supersets"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Support for <a href="/wiki/Comment_(computer_programming)" title="Comment (computer programming)">comments</a> and other features have been deemed useful, which has led to several nonstandard JSON <a href="/wiki/Superset" class="mw-redirect" title="Superset">supersets</a> being created. Among them are HJSON,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> HOCON, and JSON5 (which despite its name, is not the fifth version of JSON).<sup id="cite_ref-lucidchart_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lucidchart-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="YAML">YAML</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: YAML"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/YAML#JSON" title="YAML">YAML §&#160;JSON</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/YAML" title="YAML">YAML</a> version 1.2 is a superset of JSON; prior versions were not strictly compatible. For example, escaping a slash <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" style="" dir="ltr">/</code> with a backslash <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-text mw-content-ltr" style="" dir="ltr">\</code> is valid in JSON, but was not valid in YAML.<sup id="cite_ref-YAML_Version_1.2_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YAML_Version_1.2-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> YAML supports comments, while JSON does not.<sup id="cite_ref-YAML_Version_1.2_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YAML_Version_1.2-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lucidchart_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lucidchart-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DouglasCrockfordComments_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DouglasCrockfordComments-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="CSON">CSON</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: CSON"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><b>CSON</b> ("<a href="/wiki/CoffeeScript" title="CoffeeScript">CoffeeScript</a> Object Notation") uses <a href="/wiki/Significant_indentation" class="mw-redirect" title="Significant indentation">significant indentation</a>, unquoted keys, and assumes an outer object declaration. It was used for configuring <a href="/wiki/GitHub" title="GitHub">GitHub</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Atom_(text_editor)" title="Atom (text editor)">Atom text editor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>There is also an unrelated project called <b>CSON</b> ("Cursive Script Object Notation") that is more syntactically similar to JSON.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="HOCON">HOCON</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: HOCON"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><b>HOCON</b> ("Human-Optimized Config Object Notation") is a format for <a href="/wiki/Human-readable" class="mw-redirect" title="Human-readable">human-readable</a> data, and a superset of JSON.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
The uses of HOCON are:
</p>
<ul><li>It is primarily used in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/Play_framework" class="mw-redirect" title="Play framework">Play framework</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and is developed by <a href="/wiki/Lightbend" class="mw-redirect" title="Lightbend">Lightbend</a>.</li>
<li>It is also supported as a configuration format for .NET projects via Akka.NET<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Puppet_(software)" title="Puppet (software)">Puppet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>TIBCO Streaming:<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> HOCON is the primary configuration file format for the TIBCO Streaming<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> family of products (StreamBase, LiveView, and Artifact Management Server) as of TIBCO Streaming Release 10.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>It is also the primary configuration file format for several subsystems of Exabeam Advanced Analytics.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jitsi" title="Jitsi">Jitsi</a> uses it as the "new" config system and <a href="/wiki/.properties" title=".properties">.properties</a>-Files as fallback<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="JSON5">JSON5</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: JSON5"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><b>JSON5</b> ("JSON5 Data Interchange Format") is an extension of JSON syntax that, just like JSON, is also valid JavaScript syntax. The specification was started in 2012 and finished in 2018 with version 1.0.0.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The main differences to JSON syntax are:
</p>
<ul><li>Optional trailing commas</li>
<li>Unquoted object keys</li>
<li>Single quoted and multiline strings</li>
<li>Additional number formats</li>
<li>Comments</li></ul>
<p>JSON5 syntax is supported in some software as an extension of JSON syntax, for instance in <a href="/wiki/SQLite" title="SQLite">SQLite</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="JSONC">JSONC</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: JSONC"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><b>JSONC</b> (JSON with Comments) is a subset of JSON5 used in Microsoft's <a href="/wiki/Visual_Studio_Code" title="Visual Studio Code">Visual Studio Code</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>supports single line comments (<code>//</code>) and block comments (<code>/* */</code>)</li>
<li>accepts trailing commas, but they are discouraged and the editor will display a warning</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Derivatives">Derivatives</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Derivatives"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Several serialization formats have been built on or from the JSON specification. Examples include 
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/GeoJSON" title="GeoJSON">GeoJSON</a>, a format designed for representing simple geographical features<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/JSON-LD" title="JSON-LD">JSON-LD</a>, a method of encoding <a href="/wiki/Linked_data" title="Linked data">linked data</a> using JSON<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JSON-RPC" title="JSON-RPC">JSON-RPC</a>, a remote procedure call protocol encoded in JSON<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JsonML" title="JsonML">JsonML</a>, a lightweight markup language used to map between <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> and JSON<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Smile_(data_interchange_format)" title="Smile (data interchange format)">Smile (data interchange format)</a><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/UBJSON" title="UBJSON">UBJSON</a>, a binary computer data interchange format imitating JSON, but requiring fewer bytes of data<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JSON&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: See also"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/BSON" title="BSON">BSON</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_data_serialization_formats" class="mw-redirect" title="Comparison of data serialization formats">Comparison of data serialization formats</a></li>
<li>Amazon <a href="/wiki/Ion_(serialization_format)" title="Ion (serialization format)">Ion</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32; a superset of JSON (though limited to <a href="/wiki/UTF-8" title="UTF-8">UTF-8</a>, like JSON for interchange, unlike general JSON)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jackson_(API)" title="Jackson (API)">Jackson (API)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jaql" title="Jaql">jaql</a> – a functional data processing and query language most commonly used for JSON query processing</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jq_(programming_language)" title="Jq (programming language)">jq</a> – a "JSON query language" and high-level programming language</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JSONiq" title="JSONiq">JSONiq</a> – a JSON-oriented query and processing language based on <a href="/wiki/XQuery" title="XQuery">XQuery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JSON_streaming" title="JSON streaming">JSON streaming</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/S-expression" title="S-expression">S-expression</a></li></ul>

<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#ecma2017">ECMA-404, 2nd ed.</a>, p.&#160;3: "The JSON syntax does not impose any restrictions on the strings used as names, does not require that name strings be unique, and does not assign any significance to the ordering of name/value pairs."</span>

<li id="cite_note-DouglasCrockfordComments-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-DouglasCrockfordComments_22-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DouglasCrockfordComments_22-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DouglasCrockfordComments_22-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DouglasCrockfordComments_22-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-DouglasCrockfordComments_22-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222" /><cite id="CITEREFCrockford2012" class="citation web cs1">Crockford, Douglas (April 30, 2012). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.today/20150704102718/https://plus.google.com/+DouglasCrockfordEsq/posts/RK8qyGVaGSr">"Comments in JSON"</a>. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://plus.google.com/+DouglasCrockfordEsq/posts/RK8qyGVaGSr">the original</a> on July 4, 2015<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 30,</span> 2019</span>. <q>I removed comments from JSON because I saw people were using them to hold parsing directives, a practice which would have destroyed interoperability. I know that the lack of comments makes some people sad, but it shouldn't. Suppose you are using JSON to keep configuration files, which you would like to annotate. Go ahead and insert all the comments you like. Then pipe it through <a href="/wiki/JSMin" class="mw-redirect" title="JSMin">JSMin</a> before handing it to your JSON parser.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Comments+in+JSON&amp;rft.date=2012-04-30&amp;rft.aulast=Crockford&amp;rft.aufirst=Douglas&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fplus.google.com%2F%2BDouglasCrockfordEsq%2Fposts%2FRK8qyGVaGSr&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJSON" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#ecma2017">ECMA-404, 2nd ed.</a>, p.&#160;iii: "The JSON syntax is not a specification of a complete data interchange. Meaningful data interchange requires agreement between a producer and consumer on the semantics attached to a particular use of the JSON syntax.
